  Sandbox Orders tab — what the user will see

  A clean light-grey page with a sticky white header (Shop**Base** logo, user
  dropdown showing "Demo User", a black "🛒 Cart 0" button, "Sandbox v1.0"
  pill). Below the header, three tabs: Products / Orders / Users. On the Orders
  tab, an action bar with "+ Place Order" button (blue), then a white table with
  7 columns. Four rows visible after first load:

  #1  Demo User      Codex Smart Coffee Mug      2   $99.98   Completed   just
  now
  #2  Guest User     Developer Desk Lamp         1   $59.99   Completed   just
  now
  #3  Alex Chen      Mechanical Keyboard Pro     1   $129.00  Completed   just
  now
  #4  Demo User      Noise Cancelling Earbuds    1   $89.00   Completed   just
  now

  User cell shows name in bold with email below in grey monospace. ID cells get
  blue pills. Status gets a green "Completed" pill. Clicking "Place Order" opens
  a centered modal with a product dropdown and quantity input; on submit, a
  toast slides up from the bottom-right and the table refreshes.

  JUST ADDED banner behavior

  When Apply Slice fires for ratings, within 3 seconds the sandbox page shows a
  white card at the top with a left-side cyan-blue accent bar:

  ⚡  Add A Ratings And Reviews System  [JUST ADDED]
  /api/add-a-ratings-and-reviews-system

  The card slides down with a fade-in animation. On Reset, the card disappears
  on the next 3-second poll. Multiple features stack as separate cards.

  Studio iframe border styling

  The Studio's SandboxPreview panel previously used #060a0f (very dark navy) as
  the iframe fallback background — now #000000. The light sandbox iframe
  (#f8fafc) has its own white header so the seam between Studio's jet-black
  panel border (#1e2d3d) and the iframe's top-left corner reads as a clean 1px
  dark line against light. No visible color clashing; the contrast is
  intentional and crisp.

  Cold start time

  All three servers up + healthy after npm run dev in ~7s. POST a new order,
  trigger Synthesize→Apply→Reset cycle, verify banner appears+clears — all clean
  in under 15s.

  Stopping here. Ready to return to Phase 5 polish if/when needed.

❯ # Workbench Studio v1.1 — Sandbox React Migration PRD                         
  ## Interactive React Sandbox with Dynamic Component Loading                   
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
                                                                                
  ## Objective                                                                  
                                                                                
  Replace the vanilla HTML sandbox frontend with a fully interactive React      
  application that dynamically imports and renders Codex-generated components.  
  When Apply Slice writes a `.jsx` file to disk, the sandbox detects it,        
  imports it, and renders it live — no manual intervention, no fake banners.    
  Every layer of the generated vertical slice becomes visible and usable.       
                                                                                
  This is the most technically ambitious change in the project and the one that 
  makes the demo honest end to end.                                             
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
                                                                                
  ## Prerequisites                                                              
                                                                                
  The Express API server in `sandbox/server.js` must be fully working with all  
  endpoints from the Sandbox Rebuild PRD. Verify:                               
                                                                                
  ```bash                                                                       
  curl http://localhost:5000/api/products  # four products                      
  curl http://localhost:5000/api/orders    # seeded orders with joined data     
  curl http://localhost:5000/api/users     # seeded users                       
  curl http://localhost:5000/api/features  # empty array []                     
  curl http://localhost:5000/api/health    # { status: ok }                     
  ```                                                                           
                                                                                
  All five must return valid JSON before starting.                              
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
                                                                                
  ## Architecture Overview                                                      
                                                                                
  After this PRD the sandbox has two separate processes:                        
                                                                                
  ```                                                                           
  sandbox/                                                                      
  ├── server.js                   — Express API, unchanged, port 5000           
  ├── schema.sql                  — unchanged                                   
  ├── db.js                       — unchanged                                   
  ├── package.json                — unchanged (Express deps)                    
  └── client/                     — NEW: React + Vite frontend                  
      ├── src/                                                                  
      │   ├── main.jsx                                                          
      │   ├── App.jsx                                                           
      │   ├── components/                                                       
      │   │   ├── Header.jsx                                                    
      │   │   ├── ProductGrid.jsx                                               
      │   │   ├── CartPanel.jsx                                                 
      │   │   ├── OrdersTab.jsx                                                 
      │   │   ├── UsersTab.jsx                                                  
      │   │   └── FeatureSlot.jsx     — dynamically imports generated           
  components                                                                    
      │   ├── generated/              — Codex writes .jsx files here            
      │   │   └── .gitkeep                                                      
      │   └── index.css                                                         
      ├── index.html                                                            
      ├── vite.config.js                                                        
      └── package.json                                                          
  ```                                                                           
                                                                                
  The client Vite dev server runs on port 5001. It proxies all `/api` requests  
  to the Express server on port 5000. The Studio iframe points at port 5001     
  instead of 5000.                                                              
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
                                                                                
  ## Port Update                                                                
                                                                                
  Before building anything, update the following:                               
                                                                                
  In `studio/src/components/SandboxPreview.jsx` change the iframe src:          
  ```jsx                                                                        
  // Change from                                                                
  src="http://localhost:5000"                                                   
  // To                                                                         
  src="http://localhost:5001"                                                   
  ```                                                                           
                                                                                
  In `agent/index.js` update the reload signal target:                          
  ```javascript                                                                 
  // Change from                                                                
  fetch('http://localhost:500

      3 function timeAgo(dateStr) {
      4   const diff = (Date.now() - new Date(dateStr).getTime()) / 1000;
      5   if (diff < 60)    return 'just now';
      6   if (diff < 3600)  return Math.floor(diff / 60)   + 'm ago';
      7   if (diff < 86400) return Math.floor(diff / 3600) + 'h ago';
      8   return new Date(dateStr).toLocaleDateString();

      4   const diff = (Date.now() - new Date(dateStr).getTime()) / 1000;
      5   if (diff < 60)    return 'just now';
      6   if (diff < 3600)  return Math.floor(diff / 60)   + 'm ago';
      7   if (diff < 86400) return Math.floor(diff / 3600) + 'h ago';
      8   return new Date(dateStr).toLocaleDateString();
      9 }

     Final Pre-Ship Checks — Workbench Studio v1.1

     Context

     The product works end-to-end (verified across Phases 0–5: cold-start npm 
     run dev → all 4 servers up → Synthesize → Apply → live React component
     mount → Reset → clean state in ~15 s). The remaining gap is that the repo
     on disk is not in a state where a stranger can clone it and have it work.
     This plan closes that gap so the repo is GitHub/webapp-ready.

     The scope is repo hygiene + documentation, not new features. No code paths
     change. No agent or sandbox behavior changes.

     What the audit found

     Not bugs (no action needed)

     - SSE event names align. agent/index.js:136 emits agent-error;
     studio/src/hooks/useSSE.js:51 listens for agent-error. The recent useSSE
     edit + the handledErrorRef guard correctly separate clean agent failures
     from raw connection drops.
     - localhost:5000 references are correct where they appear. Agent → sandbox
     /api/reload (agent/index.js:156,183) and Vite proxy target
     (sandbox/client/vite.config.js:10) both legitimately point at the Express
     API on :5000. The Studio iframe and the URL chip already point at :5001.
     - console.logs in app code are intentional (startup banners + cache-hit
     log). Only matches in sandbox/server.js:148,155,190 and
     agent/index.js:54,218,219. All others are inside node_modules/ or
     studio/dist/.
     - All 4 servers wired into root package.json npm run dev.
     - sandbox/client/src/generated/.gitkeep exists, so the directory survives a
     clone-with-no-generated-components.
     - No secrets in source. Only studio/.env.local contains
     VITE_AGENT_URL=http://localhost:4000, which is non-secret config but still
     shouldn't be committed by convention.

     Blockers — must fix before the repo is shareable

     1. Runtime artifacts sitting in source tree that will be picked up by git 
     add .:
       - sandbox/add-a-ratings-and-reviews-system.migration.sql
       - sandbox/add-a-ratings-and-reviews-system.model.js
       - sandbox/add-a-ratings-and-reviews-system.routes.js
       -
     sandbox/client/src/generated/add-a-ratings-and-reviews-system.component.jsx
       - sandbox/sandbox.db (already covered by *.db)
       - studio/dist/ (already covered by dist/)
       - studio/.env.local (not covered)
     2. .gitignore is too thin. Current contents are just node_modules/, *.db,
     *.db-journal, dist/, .DS_Store. It must also exclude env files, build/Vite
     caches, logs, and the agent-generated artifact patterns so that anyone
     running a demo doesn't dirty their working copy.
     3. README is out of date. It says "Three applications" but it's now four.
     The setup step is wrong (no cd sandbox/client && npm install), the
     architecture section omits port :5001 and the React client, and the tech
     stack list doesn't mention the new sandbox client.
     4. agent/cache/ has 3 junk files from earlier live-mode autosaves with
     overlong slugified names (including a typo: add-a-referal-system-...). They
     confuse a reader skimming the cache directory.

     Polish — nice to have, not required

     - Vite scaffold leftovers in sandbox/client/src/: App.css, assets/hero.png,
     assets/react.svg, assets/vite.svg are unimported dead files. Harmless but
     messy.
     - No LICENSE file. Optional for a hackathon, recommended for any public
     repo. MIT is a safe default.
     - PRODUCT.md references localhost:5000 for the iframe (lines 85, 599) —
     it's now :5001. PRODUCT.md is a historical spec document; either annotate
     or leave as-is.
     - Subpackage package.json files lack description/author/license metadata.
     Cosmetic.
     - README's cd workbench-studio doesn't match the on-disk directory 
     dev_studio_v1. Either the GitHub repo should be named workbench-studio and
     the user clones into that name, or the README should reflect whatever name
     the repo ends up with.

     Plan

     Execute in this order:

     Step 1 — Replace .gitignore

     Path: .gitignore (repo root).

     Add the missing patterns. New full contents:
     # deps
     node_modules/

     !sandbox/client/src/generated/.gitkeep

     Step 2 — Clean runtime artifacts on disk

     These are not edits to source; they are file deletions. Run before the
     first push so they don't end up in repo history:

     - sandbox/add-a-ratings-and-reviews-system.migration.sql
     - sandbox/add-a-ratings-and-reviews-system.model.js

     Step 3 — Prune agent/cache/ to the 4 supported scenarios

     Keep:
     - add-a-ratings-and-reviews-system.json (primary, slug-matched)
     - add-a-referral-system.json (primary, slug-matched)
     - ratings-reviews.json (friendly alias)
     - referral-system.json (friendly alias)

     Delete:

     - add-a-feature-where-user-with-atleast-1-item-in-their-cart-get-a-claim-5-
     discount-option-at-checkout.json

     Step 4 — Rewrite README.md

     Same skeleton but matching today's architecture. Critical edits:

     - "Three applications" → "Four applications" with the ports correctly
     listed:
       - Workbench Studio (React + Vite) — :3000
       - Agent Engine (Node + Express + Codex CLI spawn) — :4000
       - Sandbox API (Express + SQLite) — :5000
       - Sandbox Client (React + Vite, light theme) — :5001
     - Setup block must include a step that runs npm install inside
     sandbox/client/.
     - One-line note that the Studio iframe points at :5001, which proxies /api
     to :5000.
     - Tech-stack list: add the sandbox client (React 18 + Vite 5 + Tailwind v3
     + inline styles).
     - Replace cd workbench-studio with whatever the final repo directory will
     be (likely dev_studio_v1 until the repo is renamed). Suggested: change to
     cd dev_studio_v1 and note in passing that the folder name depends on how
     the repo is cloned.
     - Keep [Insert demo video link here] placeholder — replacing it is a manual
     ship-day step.

     Step 5 — Add LICENSE (recommended)

     Drop a standard MIT LICENSE at repo root with the user's name and 2026.
     Optional but converts the repo from "code on the internet" to "code anyone
     can use," which matters for a public hackathon submission.

     Step 6 — Add .env.example at repo root (optional)

     A documentation placeholder so a fresh cloner can see what env vars exist
     without having to read source. The only one in play today is
     studio/.env.local's VITE_AGENT_URL, and the agent + Codex CLI need no env
     vars (Codex CLI handles its own auth). A minimal .env.example:
     # Studio frontend → Agent base URL (optional; defaults to
     http://localhost:4000)
     # Copy to studio/.env.local
     VITE_AGENT_URL=http://localhost:4000

     Files modified by this plan

     - .gitignore (replace)
     - README.md (rewrite)

     Verification

     After applying the plan, before the first push:

     1. Clean-clone smoke test. Tar+extract the repo to a different folder (or
     git clone from a local bare). Run:
     npm install
     cd sandbox        && npm install
     cd ../agent       && npm install
     cd ../studio      && npm install
     cd ../sandbox/client && npm install
     cd ../..
     npm run dev
     1. Confirm all four servers come up and localhost:3000 renders the dark
     Studio, localhost:5001 renders ShopBase light theme. The Studio iframe
     inside :3000 should show the ShopBase app served from :5001.
     2. Demo flow on the clean clone.
       - Click "Add Ratings & Reviews" → Synthesize Slice (Demo mode).
       - 3 SSE events stream into the Thinking Console, 4 file tabs appear in
     the diff viewer.
       - Click Apply Slice. Within ~5 s the sandbox iframe shows a "JUST ADDED ·
     Add A Ratings And Reviews System" card with a working star-rating form.
       - Submit a 5-star review with text → it appears in the list below.
       - Click Reset Sandbox in the Studio header. Within 3 s the card
     disappears from the iframe and /api/reviews returns 404.
     3. git status cleanliness. After running the full demo flow (which writes
     files to sandbox/ and sandbox/client/src/generated/ and creates
     sandbox/sandbox.db), git status must show no modified or untracked files.
     If anything shows up, the .gitignore rule for that pattern is missing.
     4. No leftover secrets. Final grep before push:
     git grep -nE 'sk-[A-Za-z0-9]{20,}|OPENAI_API_KEY=[^=].+|AUTH_TOKEN=[^=].+'
     4. should return nothing.
